Batil and Fasid Nikah: Same Ruling on Mahr
Clarifies equivalence of batil and fasid in nikah and post-dakhul distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that batil and fasid nikah are treated alike in Hanafi law regarding mahr, and apply the distribution rule when both a valid and a fasid marriage are involved.

Core Idea
In nikah, batil and fasid are synonymous; after dakhul, mahr al-mithl is wajib in both.

You have learned that in sales, batil (void) and fasid (defective) have distinct effects. But in marriage, Hanafi law treats them identically when it comes to the wife's right to mahr after consummation. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains this key difference and also handles a complex scenario where one marriage is valid and the other fasid, and the identities are unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on batil and fasid in nikah
The passage states that in nikah, there is no distinction between batil and fasid. Both are treated the same regarding the obligation of mahr after dakhul. Focus on the phrase 'لا فرق في النكاح بين الباطل والفاسد'.
This is contrary to other transactions where batil is void ab initio and fasid is voidable.
2
Distinguish rulings before and after dakhul
If separation occurs before consummation, no mahr is due. After consummation, mahr al-mithl (or the 'uqr, which is the lesser of specified mahr and mahr al-mithl) becomes wajib. Note that the text says 'يجب مهر المثل' for batil and fasid alike.
The term 'uqr is used specifically for fasid nikah to indicate the lesser amount.
3
Understand the 'uqr (dower in fasid nikah)
The 'uqr is defined as the lesser of the specified mahr (musamma) and mahr al-mithl. In a scenario where one marriage is valid and the other fasid, the valid wife gets the full specified mahr, and the fasid wife gets the 'uqr.
This avoids giving a wife more than what was agreed or the customary mahr.
4
Analyze the distribution when identities are unknown
When it is unknown which wife was in the valid marriage and which in the fasid one, the two mahr amounts (the specified mahr from the valid marriage and the 'uqr from the fasid) are distributed between the two women. The text gives four scenarios based on whether the specified mahrs and actual mahrs are equal or different.
The method from Radd al-Muhtar ensures each woman gets at least the minimum she is entitled to.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1]قوله : باطل ؛ ذكر في «الفتح») ، وغيره : أنه لا فرق في النكاح بين الباطل والفاسد ، وأن في مثله يجب مهر المثل بعد الدخول، ففي صورة التفريق قبل الدخول لا يجب شيء. قوله : وقد فارق الأولى ... الخ ؛ الواو حالية، وأشار به إلى أن الحكم المذكور فيما إذا فَرَّقَ بينه وبينهما قبل الدخول بكلِّ منهما ، وأما إذا كانت الفرقة بعد الدخول، فذكر في «الفتح» و«البحر»(۳) وغيرهما ما حاصله : أنه لما كان أحد النكاحين في مسألة النسيان صحيحاً، والآخر فاسداً، وبعد الدخول يجب في الصحيح كل المسمى، وفي الفاسد العقر: أي الأقل من المسمى ومن مهر المثل، فحيث لم تُعْلَمْ صاحبةُ الصحيح من صاحبة الفاسد يقسم المهران بالوصف المذكور بينهما، فيكون لكل واحدة مهر كامل. وذكر في رد المحتار) نقلاً عن شيخه أنه حيث جهل ذات الصحيح وذات الفاسد، وكان لإحداهما المسمّى وللأخرى العقر ، فلهما أن يأخذا المتيقن ويقتسمانه في الصور الأربع، فإذا اتحد المسمّيان والمهران يعطيان أحد المسميين وأحد المهرين. وإذا اتحد الأولان فقط يعطيان أحد المسمّيين وأقلّ المهرين، وإذا اختلف الأولان فقط يعطيان أقل المسمّيين وأحد المهرين، وإذا اختلف الأولان والأخيران يعطيان أقل المسمّيين وأقل المهرين، وفي المقام تفصيل واختلاف مبسوط في حواشي «الدر المختار».
[1] His statement: 'invalid' – it is mentioned in al-Fath and others that there is no difference in marriage between the invalid (batil) and the defective (fasid), and that in its like mahr al-mithl is obligatory after consummation. So in the case of separation before consummation, nothing is obligatory. His statement: 'and he separated from the first... etc.' – the waw is circumstantial, and he indicated by it that the mentioned ruling is when he separated from both of them before consummation with each one. But if the separation was after consummation, it is mentioned in al-Fath and al-Bahr and others what amounts to: since one of the two marriages in the case of forgetfulness is valid and the other defective, and after consummation in the valid one all the specified mahr is obligatory, and in the defective one the uqr (i.e., the lesser of the specified mahr and mahr al-mithl). So when the woman of the valid and the woman of the defective are not known, the two mahrs with the described description are divided between them, so each has a full mahr. It is mentioned in Radd al-Muhtar quoting his teacher that when the woman of the valid and the woman of the defective are unknown, and one has the specified mahr and the other the uqr, they may take the certain amount and divide it in the four situations. If the two specified mahrs and the two actual mahrs are equal, they give one of the specified mahrs and one of the actual mahrs. If only the first two are equal, they give one of the specified mahrs and the lesser of the two actual mahrs. If only the last two are equal, they give the lesser of the two specified mahrs and one of the actual mahrs. If both the first two and last two differ, they give the lesser of the specified mahrs and the lesser of the actual mahrs. There is detailed elaboration and difference in the margins of al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two phrases from the matn. First, it clarifies the term 'batil' (invalid) in the context of marriage. The commentator notes that according to Fath al-Qadir and others, there is no distinction in nikah between batil and fasid (defective); both are treated the same regarding mahr. After consummation (dakhul), mahr al-mithl is due in both cases; before consummation, nothing is due. This is important because in other areas of fiqh (like sales), batil and fasid have different rulings, but in marriage they are synonymous. Second, the passage discusses the ruling when separation occurs after consummation in the earlier case of forgotten priority. When one marriage is valid and the other fasid (due to forgetfulness of which was first), after dakhul the valid marriage requires the full specified mahr, while the fasid requires the 'uqr (the lesser of the specified mahr and mahr al-mithl). Since the women's identities are unknown, the two mahrs are divided between them, each receiving a full mahr (one gets the specified mahr, the other gets the uqr). However, a more precise method from Radd al-Muhtar based on his teacher's view is then given: the women take the certain amount and divide it according to four possible scenarios depending on whether the specified mahrs and actual mahrs are equal or different. These scenarios ensure that each woman receives at least the minimum she is entitled to.

Key Terms
الباطل (al-batil): An invalid marriage contract that never produces legal effects; in nikah, it is treated like fasid.
الفاسد (al-fasid): A defective marriage contract; in nikah, it is equivalent to batil, requiring mahr after dakhul but not before.
العقر (al-'uqr): The dower due in a fasid marriage after consummation; it is the lesser of the specified mahr and mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only a mut'ah gift

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, batil and fasid nikah are identical in requiring mahr al-mithl after consummation, and before consummation no mahr is due.

Mahr Division When Marriage Validity is Unknown
Explanation of mahr division when marriage validity is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for mahr distribution when one of two marriages is valid and the identity is unknown, and evaluate the internal Hanafi dispute on the batil/fasid distinction in nikah.

Core Idea
Half mahr divides equally before consummation; after, each wife gets her due based on named mahr and 'uqr.

This passage addresses a delicate scenario: a man marries two women but forgets which marriage was valid and which was invalid (fasid). How is the mahr distributed when the identity of the valid wife is unknown? The answer depends on whether separation occurred before or after consummation, and on a nuanced understanding of the terms 'batil' and 'fasid' in Hanafi nikah. We'll walk through the rulings and the internal debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The core issue: two marriages, one valid and one invalid, but the identity of the valid wife is unknown. The ruling must allocate mahr fairly between the two women.
The ruling differs before and after consummation.
2
Apply mahr rules before consummation
In a valid marriage, half the named mahr is wajib before consummation. In an invalid marriage, no mahr is due. Since the identity is unknown, the half mahr is divided equally between the two women.
Each woman receives one-quarter of the named mahr.
3
Apply mahr rules after consummation
After consummation, the valid wife receives the full named mahr; the invalid wife receives the 'uqr (the lesser of the named mahr and mahr al-mithl). Since identity is unknown, the two mahr amounts are distributed based on four scenarios (Radd al-Muhtar).
The scenarios depend on whether the named mahr amounts and mahr al-mithl amounts are the same or different.
4
Understand the batil/fasid distinction dispute
The mashhur Hanafi position is that there is no distinction between batil and fasid in nikah; the terms are used interchangeably. Some later scholars (al-Zahidi, Ibn Nujaym) differentiate, but the majority view is mufta bihi.
This is terminological; the practical rulings are the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد فارق الأولى قبل الوطء، فيجب نصف المهر، ولا يدري لمن هو، فينصف المهر بينهما. قوله: وقد فارق الأولى... الخ؛ الواو حالية، وأشار به إلى أن الحكم المذكور فيما إذا فرق بينه وبينهما قبل الدخول بكل منهما، وأما إذا كانت الفرقة بعد الدخول، فذكر في الفتح والبحر وغيرهما ما حاصله: أنه لما كان أحد النكاحين في مسألة النسيان صحيحاً، والآخر فاسداً، وبعد الدخول يجب في الصحيح كل المسمى، وفي الفاسد العقر: أي الأقل من المسمى ومن مهر المثل، فحيث لم تعلم صاحبة الصحيح من صاحبة الفاسد يقسم المهران بالوصف المذكور بينهما، فيكون لكل واحدة مهر كامل. وذكر في رد المحتار نقلاً عن شيخه أنه حيث جهل ذات الصحيح وذات الفاسد، وكان لإحداهما المسمى وللأخرى العقر، فلهما أن يأخذا المتيقن ويقتسمانه في الصور الأربع، فإذا اتحد المسميان والمهران يعطيان أحد المسميين وأحد المهرين. وإذا اتحد الأولان فقط يعطيان أحد المسميين وأقل المهرين، وإذا اختلف الأولان فقط يعطيان أقل المسميين وأحد المهرين، وإذا اختلف الأولان والأخيران يعطيان أقل المسميين وأقل المهرين، وفي المقام تفصيل واختلاف مبسوط في حواشي الدر المختار. من المشهور أنه لا فرق بين النكاح الباطل والفاسد في النكاح، بل كل لفظ منهما يستخدم بدل الآخر، وعلى عدم التفريق عبارات عامة الكتب، وبذلك صرح ابن الهمام في فتح القدير (٣: ٢٤٣)، فقال: لا فرق بينهما في النكاح بخلاف البيع، إلا أن الزاهدي فرق بينهما وتابعه ابن نجيم في البحر الرائق (٤: ١٥٦) ومشى على ذلك ابن عابدين في... ولا ضير في ذلك؛ إذ أنه اصطلاح. قوله: فلا يجب شيء من المهر؛ هذا إذا كان التفريق قبل الدخول؛ وذلك لأن في صورة النسيان صح نكاح السابقة دون اللاحقة، وتعين التفريق بينهما للجهل بحال السابقة، والتي صح نكاحها يجب لها نصف المهر قبل الدخول، ولما جهلت انقسم عليهما. بخلاف ما إذا تزوجهما معاً، فإن كلا من النكاحين فيه باطل، فإذا كان التفريق قبل الدخول فلا مهر لهما ولا عدة عليهما، وأما إن دخل بهما وجب لكل الأقل من المسمى ومن مهر المثل، وعليهما العدة. كذا في البحر الرائق.
And he separated from the first [wife] before intercourse, so half the mahr is obligatory, and it is not known to whom it belongs, so the mahr is divided in half between them. He said: 'And he separated from the first...' etc.; the waw is circumstantial, and he indicated by this that the mentioned ruling applies when he separates from both of them before entering with each. But if the separation is after entering, then it is mentioned in al-Fath and al-Bahr and others that the summary is: Since one of the two marriages in the case of forgetfulness is valid and the other invalid, after entering the full named mahr is obligatory in the valid one, and in the invalid one the 'uqr (i.e., the lesser of the named mahr and the mahr al-mithl). So when the owner of the valid marriage is not known from the owner of the invalid, the two mahr amounts are divided between them according to the described description, so each will have a full mahr. And it is mentioned in Radd al-Muhtar, quoting his teacher, that when the identity of the valid and invalid is unknown, and one woman has the named mahr and the other the 'uqr, they may take the certain and divide it in four scenarios: if the named amounts and the mahr amounts are identical, they are given one named amount and one mahr amount; if only the first two are identical, they are given one named amount and the lesser of the two mahr amounts; if only the first two differ, they are given the lesser of the two named amounts and one mahr amount; if both the first and last differ, they are given the lesser of the two named amounts and the lesser of the two mahr amounts. In this topic there is detailed discussion and difference of opinion in the glosses of al-Durr al-Mukhtar. It is well-known that there is no difference between a batil and fasid marriage in nikah; rather each term is used interchangeably. The general expressions of the books indicate no differentiation, and Ibn al-Humam stated this in Fath al-Qadir (3:243), saying: There is no difference between them in nikah unlike in sales, except that al-Zahidi differentiated between them and Ibn Nujaym followed him in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (4:156), and Ibn Abidin proceeded on that... and there is no harm in that since it is a matter of terminology. He said: 'So nothing of the mahr is obligatory'; this is when the separation is before entering; that is because in the case of forgetfulness, the marriage of the earlier one is valid and not the later, and separation between them is necessary due to ignorance of the identity of the earlier one. The one whose marriage is valid is entitled to half the mahr before entering, and since she is unknown, it is divided between them. In contrast, if he married both simultaneously, then both marriages are batil. So if separation is before entering, there is no mahr for them nor 'iddah; but if he entered with them, each is obliged the lesser of the named mahr and the mahr al-mithl, and they must observe 'iddah. This is stated in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a man who marries two women but forgets which marriage was valid and which was invalid (fasid). The commentator explains the ruling based on the matn: if he separates from both before consummation, half the mahr is due but it is unknown to whom, so it is divided equally. After consummation, the valid marriage gives the full named mahr, and the invalid gives the 'uqr (the lesser of the named mahr and the proper mahr). Since the identities are unknown, the two mahr amounts are assigned based on certain scenarios described in detail from Radd al-Muhtar. The passage also clarifies a Hanafi internal dispute: the majority (including Ibn al-Humam) hold that there is no difference between batil and fasid in nikah, even though some later scholars distinguished them. The commentary then clarifies a sub-case: when the marriage was done with one contract instead of two, both marriages are batil, so no mahr or 'iddah if separated before consummation, but after consummation each gets the lesser amount and must observe 'iddah.

Key Terms
النكاح الباطل (al-nikah al-batil): A marriage that is void ab initio due to a fundamental defect (e.g., marrying a mahram).
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage that is voidable due to a defect (e.g., missing a witness).
العقر (al-‘uqr): The mahr due in an invalid marriage after consummation: the lesser of the named mahr and the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of forgetfulness (nisyan) where a man married two women, one valid and one invalid, and separated from both before consummation, how is the half mahr distributed?
A) It is given entirely to the valid wife.
B) It is divided equally between the two women.
C) It is not due because both marriages are invalid.
D) It is given entirely to the invalid wife.

Key Takeaway
When marriage validity is unknown, mahr is distributed based on the known minimums, and the Hanafi school treats batil and fasid as synonymous in nikah.

Prohibition of Marrying Two Women Mahram to Each Other
Ruling with proof on combining women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule on combining two women in marriage, identify the exception for stepdaughter, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Marrying two women who would be mahram if male is haram, but stepdaughter is an exception because the prohibition is not mutual.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya establishes a key principle in marriage law: you may not simultaneously marry two women who would be mahram to each other if they were male. However, there is an important exception for stepdaughters, which sparked a well-known debate within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar. Let us examine the rule, the exception, and the reasoning behind the majority position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Prohibition
The matn states that combining two women such that if each were male, the other would be unlawful (mahram) is prohibited. This covers cases like two sisters or a woman and her aunt.
The condition is hypothetical: if both were male, they would be in a prohibited relationship (e.g., two sisters would be brother and brother? No, it means if they were male, they would be related in a way that prohibits marriage, like a man and his sister).
2
Understand the Exception
The exception is for a woman and her husband's daughter from another wife (stepdaughter). The reasoning: if the stepdaughter were male, she would be the husband's son, but the other woman would not become his mahram through that hypothetical.
The prohibition requires mutual hypothetical mahramiyya, which is missing here.
3
Analyze Zufar's Objection
Imam Zufar argued that if the stepdaughter were male, she would be the husband's son, making the woman his father's wife, hence prohibited. He viewed the condition from one side only.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The majority Hanafi response is that the condition must be bilateral: both women must become mahram to one another if male. Since the stepdaughter's mother does not become mahram to the stepdaughter (if male), the combination is permissible.
This is supported by the practice of Companions.
5
Review the Supporting Evidence
The commentator cites that Abdullah ibn Ja'far and Ibn Abbas practiced such a combination, recorded by Bukhari and al-Daraqutni. This strengthens the majority view.
These are ahadith, not Quranic verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع بين امرأتين أيتهما فرضت ذكراً لم تحل له الأخرى، لا بين امرأة وبنت زوجها لا منها؛ لأن بنت الزوج لو فرضت ذكراً كان ابن الزوج، وهو حرام، أما المرأة الأخرى لو فرضت ذكراً لا تحرم عليه تلك المرأة. وصح. قوله: لا بين... الخ؛ أي لا يحرم الجمع بين امرأة وبنت زوجها من زوجته الأخرى، ومنعه زفر بناءً على أن بنت الزوج لو قدرتها ذكرا يحرم عليه التزوج بتلك المرأة لكونها امرأة أبيه. ونحن نقول الشرط: أن يتصور هذا من الجانبين، وهو مفقود هاهنا من الجانب الآخر، وقد صح أن عبد الله بن جعفر جمع بين امرأة علي وابنته، ذكره البخاري، وعن ابن عباس: أنه جمع بين امرأة رجل وابنته من غيرها، أخرجه الدارقطني، وكذلك أخرجه عن صحابي من أهل مصر يقال له جلة. كذا في البناية. قوله: وصح؛ الأصل في هذا الباب قوله: (اليوم أحل لكم الطيبات)
And combining two women such that if each were assumed male, the other would not be lawful for him [is prohibited], except [the combination of] a woman and her husband's daughter from another [wife]; because if the husband's daughter were assumed male, she would be [like] the husband's son, and he is forbidden, but the other woman, if assumed male, she does not become forbidden to that woman. And it is valid. He said: 'Except...' meaning it is not prohibited to combine a woman and her husband's daughter from his other wife. Zufar prohibited it based on the reasoning that if the husband's daughter were considered male, he would be prohibited from marrying that woman because she would be his father's wife. But we say: the condition is that this [relation] is conceivable from both sides, and it is absent here from the other side. It is authentically reported that Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined the wife of Ali and his daughter, as mentioned by Bukhari; and from Ibn Abbas that he combined a man's wife and his daughter from another [wife], narrated by al-Daraqutni, and similarly from a companion from Egypt called Jilla. This is in al-Binaya. He said: 'And it is valid'; the basis in this chapter is His statement: 'Today good things are made lawful for you...'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prohibition of combining two women in marriage when each would be forbidden to the other if they were male (e.g., two sisters). The matn states the general rule and then excepts the case of a woman and her husband's daughter from another wife (stepdaughter). The commentator explains that the exception is because if the stepdaughter were male, she would be the husband's son, who is a mahram, but the other woman (the stepdaughter's mother) would not become forbidden to the stepdaughter if the stepdaughter were male. The commentator then addresses an objection by Imam Zufar, who considered such a combination prohibited because if the stepdaughter were male, she would be a son, and the other woman would be the father's wife, thus forbidden. The Hanafi response is that the condition for prohibition is that the relationship be mutual: both women must be mahram to each other if male. In this case, only one side applies. The passage supports the Hanafi permissibility with the practice of Abdullah ibn Ja'far and Ibn Abbas, as recorded in authentic hadith collections. Finally, it notes that the general principle is the Quranic verse about lawful things, implying the default permissibility unless prohibited by explicit text.

Key Terms
الجمع بين امرأتين (al-jam‘ bayna imra’atayn): Marrying two women simultaneously who are related in a way that would make one forbidden to the other if they were male.
بنت الزوج لا منها (bint al-zawj la minha): The husband's daughter from another wife (stepdaughter), who is not a mahram to the woman he is marrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason that marrying a woman and her stepdaughter (her husband's daughter from another wife) is permissible?
A) Because the stepdaughter is not related by blood to the woman.
B) Because the condition of mutual hypothetical mahramiyya is not fulfilled.
C) Because the stepdaughter is already a mahram to the woman.
D) Because the stepdaughter is considered a man.

Key Takeaway
The general prohibition of combining two women in marriage applies only when the hypothetical mahram relation is mutual; the stepdaughter exception is a key example where mutuality fails, making the combination permissible.

Marriage to Kitabiyyat: Permissibility and Repugnance
Ruling with proof and karaha distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on marrying a Harbi Kitabiyyah from a Dhimmi Kitabiyyah and explain the basis for the different levels of karaha.

Core Idea
Marriage to a Kitabiyyah is valid but may be makruh; the degree depends on her legal status.

The Quran explicitly permits marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book, yet the Hanafi school teaches that this permission does not exclude dislike (karaha). In this lesson, we explore the distinction between two categories of Kitabiyyat—those from enemy territory (harbi) and those under Muslim protection (dhimmi)—and how the level of repugnance differs. We also examine an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the repugnance is prohibitory or merely non-prohibitory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary evidence
Locate the Quranic verse (5:5) cited in the text. Note that it uses 'halal lakum' (lawful for you) which gives a general permission for marriage to chaste Kitabiyyat.
The verse is from Surah al-Ma'idah, which is a later Medinan revelation, indicating finality of the ruling.
2
Establish the ruling of validity
Recognize that the marriage is valid (sahih) based on the explicit Quranic text. The author states 'thumma hadhihi al-sihha la tunafi al-karahah' (this validity does not negate repugnance), meaning the marriage is legally sound even if disliked.
Thus, permissibility and dislike can coexist in Hanafi hukm.
3
Distinguish harbi vs dhimmi
The text explains that for a Harbi Kitabiyyah (from dar al-harb), there is consensus on karaha due to fitna and harm to children. For a Dhimmi Kitabiyyah, the karaha is weaker.
The key difference: harbi opens the door to prolonged residence in enemy territory and potential loss of religious identity for offspring.
4
Analyze the disagreement on karaha type
The apparent meaning of the source text (Fath al-Qadeer) assigns prohibitory repugnance (tahrimiyya) to harbi and non-prohibitory (tanzihiyya) to dhimmi. However, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq chooses tanzihiyya for both.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the mufta bihi (operative position) is the tanzihiyya view from al-Bahr.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete case
Consider a scenario: a Muslim man wishes to marry a Christian woman living in a non-Muslim state. Depending on whether her country is at war with Muslims (harbi) or has a treaty/peace (dhimmi-like), the ruling differs in degree of repugnance.
The modern application requires careful legal classification of the woman's status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نكاح الكتابية
الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ حِلٌّ لَكُمْ وَطَعَامُكُمْ حِلٌّ لَهُمْ وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ وَالْمُصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الكِتَابَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ (سورة المائدة: آية 5).
ثم هذه الصحة لا تنافي الكراهة، وكذا قال في «الفتح»: «يجوز تزوج الكتابيات، والأولى أن لا يفعل، ولا تؤكل ذبيحتهم إلا للضرورة، وتكره الكتابية الحربية إجماعاً؛ لافتتاح باب الفتنة من إمكان التعلق المستدعي للمقام معها في دار الحرب، وتعريض الولد على التخلق بأخلاق أهل الكفر، وعلى الرق بأن تُسبى وهي حبلى فيولد رقيقاً وإن كان مسلماً». انتهى.
فظاهرُهُ أنَّ الكراهة في الكتابية الحربية تحريمية، وفي الدمية تنزيهية، واختار في «البحر» كونَ الكراهة فيهما تنزيهية.
قوله: نكاح الكتابية؛ أي اليهودية والنصرانية وغيرهما ممن اعتقد ديناً سماوياً، وله كتاب منزل، كصحف إبراهيم عليه السلام وشيث عليه السلام، وزبور داود عليه السلام، كذا ذكره الزيلعي. وفي إطلاقه إشارة إلى شمول الحكم للحربية والذمية، وللحرة والأمة؛ لإطلاق الآية المبيحة له، وإلى جواز النكاح بالكتابية وإن قالت بثالث ثلاثة، وقيده في «المستصفى» بأن لا يعتقد ذلك بل يكون على دينه، ويوافقه ما في «مبسوط شيخ الإسلام»: يجب أن لا يأكلوا ذبائح أهل الكتاب ولا يتزوجوا نساءهم إذا اعتقدوا أن المسيح إله وأن عزيراً إله، والصحيح جواز نكاحهم وأكل ذبائحهم مطلقاً، كما حققه.
Marriage to the Kitabiyyah. "Lawful to you are the chaste women from the believers and the chaste women from those who were given the Scripture before you" (Quran 5:5). Then this validity does not negate repugnance. Likewise it is said in Fath: 'Marrying Kitabiyyat is permissible, but it is better not to do so. Their slaughtered meat should not be eaten except out of necessity. The Harbi Kitabiyyah is repugnant by consensus, due to opening the door of fitna from the possibility of attachment requiring residence with her in dar al-harb, and exposing the child to adopting the morals of the people of disbelief, and to slavery by being captured while pregnant so the child is born a slave even if Muslim.' End. So its apparent meaning is that repugnance in the Harbi Kitabiyyah is prohibitory, and in the Dhimmiyya is non-prohibitory. In al-Bahr, he chose that repugnance in both is non-prohibitory. His statement: 'Marriage to the Kitabiyyah' refers to the Jewess, Christian, and others who believe in a heavenly religion and have a revealed book, like the Scriptures of Ibrahim (AS) and Shith (AS), and the Psalms of Dawud (AS), as al-Zayla'i mentioned. In its absolute form, it indicates inclusion of the Harbi and Dhimmi, the free and slave, due to the absolute nature of the verse permitting it, and the permissibility of marrying the Kitabiyyah even if she says 'third of three'. In al-Mustasfa, it is restricted that she not believe that but be upon her religion. Agreeing with what is in Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam: 'They must not eat the slaughtered meat of the People of the Book nor marry their women if they believe that the Messiah is God and that Uzayr is God.' The correct view is the permissibility of marrying them and eating their slaughtered meat absolutely, as he verified.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Book of Marriage on the permissibility of marrying Kitabiyyat (Jewish or Christian women). The author begins by quoting Quran 5:5, which explicitly allows marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book. He then clarifies that this validity does not preclude dislike (karaha). Citing Fath al-Qadeer, he states that marriage is permissible but it is better not to do so, and their slaughtered meat should not be eaten except in necessity. He distinguishes between the Harbi Kitabiyyah (from enemy territory), for whom there is consensus on karaha, and the Dhimmiyya (from under Muslim protection), for whom the karaha is weaker. The author then concludes from the text that the karaha for Harbi is tahrimi (prohibitive) and for Dhimmi is tanzihi (non-prohibitive), though al-Bahr chooses that both are tanzihi. He then defines the Kitabiyyah as one who believes in a heavenly religion with a revealed book, including not only Jews and Christians but also followers of earlier scriptures like those of Ibrahim and Shith. The ruling applies to both Harbi and Dhimmi, free and slave. A key issue is the Christian belief in the Trinity: despite this shirk, marriage is still permissible because the verse is unconditional. Some earlier scholars restricted it only to those who do not explicitly deify Jesus or Uzayr, but the verified correct view, as in the text, is absolute permissibility.

Key Terms
كتابية (Kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book, i.e., Jews, Christians, and others with a revealed scripture.
كراهة تحريمية (karāha taḥrīmiyya): Prohibitory repugnance: a disliked act that is closer to haram.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāha tanzīhiyya): Non-prohibitory repugnance: a disliked act that is not sinful but better avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on marrying a Harbi Kitabiyyah?
A) It is absolutely permissible.
B) It is permissible but with prohibitory repugnance (karaha tahrimiyya) according to the apparent meaning, though some choose non-prohibitory.
C) It is haram.
D) It is only permissible if she has a book.

Key Takeaway
Marriage to a Kitabiyyah is valid, but the degree of dislike differs between harbi (possibly prohibitory) and dhimmi (non-prohibitory), with the relied-upon view being non-prohibitory for both.

Marriage to Sabian Women: Conditions and Proof
Ruling with proof on Sabian marriage conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for marriage to Sabian women and apply the Quranic proof to distinguish between permissible and impermissible cases.

Core Idea
Sabian women with a scripture and belief in a prophet are treated as People of the Book; without these, they are polytheists and marriage is forbidden.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the Hanafi ruling on marrying Sabian women. The key is that not all Sabians are the same—the ruling depends on their beliefs and possession of a divine book. We will walk through the proof from Quranic verses and Hanafi reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is marriage (nikah) to a Sabian woman. The ruling is conditional: it is sahih (valid) under certain conditions and batil (void) otherwise.
2
State the two conditions for permissibility
According to the text, marriage is permissible if the Sabian woman (1) believes in a prophet and (2) acknowledges a divine book. If either is absent, she is considered a polytheist (mushrikah) and marriage is forbidden.
These are shurut (conditions) for validity, not arkan (pillars).
3
Locate the Quranic dalil
The author cites the general prohibition (al-Baqarah 2:221: 'Do not marry polytheist women') and the exception for People of the Book (al-Ma'idah 5:5: 'Permitted to you are the chaste women of those who were given the Scripture before you').
Both verses are qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalalah (open to interpretation).
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (proof link)
The verse forbidding mushrikat is specified (takhsis) by the verse permitting Kitabiyyat. Sabians with a book are included in 'those given the Scripture' because they possess a revealed text and believe in a prophet. Thus, they fall under the exception.
This is the core of the Hanafi istidlal (inference).
5
Note the ikhtilaf and its basis
Some scholars outside the Hanafi school consider all Sabians polytheists because of their star worship. The Hanafi response is that the ruling depends on their actual beliefs and possession of scripture, and the historical disagreement arises from confusion about the Sabian sect.
Al-Hidaya states: 'the disagreement is based on uncertainty about their beliefs.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصابئة المؤمنة بنبي المقرة بكتاب، لا عبادة كواكب لا كتاب لها في «الفتح»، و«البناية»، وغيرهما.
فإن أهل الكتاب كانوا يعتقدون في العصر النبوي بثالث ثلاثة وبكون عيسى وعزير ابن الله له كما حكى الله عنهم في غير موضع من القرآن، ومع ذلك أباح ذبائحهم ومناكحتهم مطلقاً.
فَعُلِمَ أن شركهم غير مانع عنه، وأن قوله: وَلَا تَنكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكَتِ مخصوص بغير الكتابيات، كيف لا واسم الشرك إذا ذكر في الشرع مطلقاً لم يتناول أهل الكتاب.
[١] قوله: والصابئة؛ من صباً إذا خرج من دين الى دين، والصابئون طائفة يعبدون الكواكب، قال في «الهداية»: «يجوز تزوج الصابئات إن كانوا يؤمنون بدين نبي ويقرون بكتاب؛ لأنهم من أهل الكتاب، وإن كانوا يعبدون الكواكب ولا كتاب معهم لم تجز مناكحتهم؛ لأنهم مشركون، والخلافُ المنقول فيه محمول على اشتباه مذهبهم، فكل أجاب على ما وقع عنده، وعلى هذا حال ذبيحتهم». انتهى.

[٣] قوله: لا كتاب لها؛ ظاهرُهُ أن عدم مناكحتهم مقيد بقيدين: عدم الكتاب...
And the Sabian woman who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a book, not a worshipper of stars without a book, according to Fath, Binaya, and others. For the People of the Book in the prophetic era believed in a 'third of three' and that Jesus and Uzayr were sons of God, as Allah narrated about them in multiple places of the Quran, yet He permitted their slaughtered meat and marriage absolutely. So it is understood that their shirk is not a barrier, and that His statement 'Do not marry polytheist women' is specific to non-Kitabiyyat. How could it not be, since the term 'shirk' when mentioned absolutely in the Shariah does not include the People of the Book. [1] His statement: 'And the Sabian'—from 'saba' when he leaves one religion for another. The Sabians are a sect that worships stars. In al-Hidaya it says: 'Marriage to Sabian women is permissible if they believe in the religion of a prophet and acknowledge a book, because they are from the People of the Book. But if they worship stars and have no book with them, their marriage is not permissible because they are polytheists. The transmitted disagreement about them is based on confusion about their sect, so each answered according to what occurred to him. The same applies to their slaughtered meat.' End. [2] His statement: 'the believer' is a descriptive attribute for the Sabian according to Abu Hanifa RA, and restrictive according to others. [3] His statement: 'no book'—its apparent meaning is that non-marriage is conditioned by two conditions: no book...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Book of Marriage concerning the permissibility of marrying Sabian women. The author first states the condition: only those Sabians who believe in a prophet and have a book are permissible; those who worship stars without a book are not. He then argues by analogy that since Christians, despite their shirk (trinitarianism), were permitted in marriage by the Quran, Sabians who have a book are similarly permitted. The verse forbidding marriage to polytheists is specific to non-Kitabiyyat. The commentary from al-Hidaya clarifies the linguistic meaning of Sabian and the ruling: if they believe in a prophet and have a book, they are treated like People of the Book; otherwise, they are polytheists and marriage is forbidden. The disagreement among scholars stems from uncertainty about Sabian beliefs. The author also notes that 'mu'minah' (believer) is descriptive for Abu Hanifa's view (meaning they are considered believers in some sense) but restrictive for others (meaning only those who are already believers). The final comment indicates that the prohibition of marriage is conditioned on two factors (absence of book and worship of stars), but the passage cuts off.

Key Terms
صابئة (Ṣābi'a): A sect that worships stars but may have a scripture; their status depends on belief in a prophet and possession of a book.
المؤمنة بنبي (al-mu'mina bi-nabiyy): One who believes in a prophet; used as a descriptive qualifier for Sabians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage to a Sabian woman only if she believes in a prophet and possesses a divine book; otherwise she is a polytheist and marriage is forbidden.

Marriage to Sabian Women: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Sabian marriage based on classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marrying Sabian women and explain the divergent views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn based on their classification.

Core Idea
Marriage to a Sabian woman hinges on her belief in a prophet and a book; Abu Hanifa permits, the Sahibayn prohibit.

This lesson examines an intra-madhhab dispute concerning the permissibility of marrying Sabian women. The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa classifies Sabians as People of the Book if they affirm a prophet and a scripture, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider them star-worshippers with no revealed book. Understanding the grounds of this disagreement helps clarify how legal rulings can vary based on factual classifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is about the permissibility of marriage (nikah) to Sabian women. The ruling depends on whether Sabians are considered Ahl al-Kitab (People of the Book) or polytheists (mushrikun).
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that if a Sabian believes in a prophet and acknowledges a scripture, she is from Ahl al-Kitab, making marriage permissible. His evidence includes Quran 2:221 (restricted to non-Scriptural polytheists) and reports that Sabians read the Psalms.
Reports from Abu al-Aliyah, al-Suddi, and Qatada cited in tafsir.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that Sabians are star-worshippers with no book, thus polytheists whose marriage is forbidden. They rely on a report from Ibn Abbas classifying them as such.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the disagreement
The dispute is attributed to confusion about the Sabian sect. Each imam ruled according to the information available to him. Later authorities suggest the difference is lexical; the practical ruling depends on the specific individual's beliefs.
Al-Durr al-Muntaqa states that if a Sabian woman affirms a prophet and book, marriage is valid by agreement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Sabian woman claims to follow a prophet and a book, her marriage is valid (Abu Hanifa) or invalid (Sahibayn). The mufta bihi leans toward permissibility, making the dispute largely semantic.

Source Text

And the Sabian woman who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a book, not a worshipper of stars without a book. In al-Fath and al-Binayah and others. For the People of the Book believed in the Prophetic era in a Trinity and that Jesus and Ezra were sons of God, as Allah related about them in more than one place in the Quran, and despite that He permitted their slaughtered animals and marriages absolutely. So it is known that their polytheism is not a barrier, and that His statement 'And do not marry polytheist women' is specific to non-Scriptural women. How not? For the term polytheism when mentioned absolutely in the Law does not include the People of the Book. He said: al-Sabi'a is from sabaa when he goes out from one religion to another, and al-Sabi'un are a group who worship stars. He said in al-Hidayah: 'It is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in the religion of a prophet and acknowledge a book because they are from the People of the Book; but if they worship stars and have no book, their marriage is not permissible because they are polytheists. The disagreement transmitted about it is based on confusion about their sect, so each responded according to what occurred to him. And the same applies to their slaughtered animals.' He said: al-Mu'minah is a clarifying description for the Sabian in the view of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and a restrictive one in the view of others. He said: 'without a book' - its apparent meaning is that prohibition of their marriage is restricted by two conditions: absence of a book and worship of stars. Know that the marriage of a Sabian woman is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, not according to the two companions. It is said: This disagreement is based on the interpretation of al-Sabi'i. Abu Hanifa claimed that the Sabian is from the People of the Book; if so, their marriage is permissible. The two companions claimed that he is a worshipper of stars and has no book; if so, her marriage is not permissible. Then he coupled with the marriage of a Scriptural woman his statement: 'and the marriage of the one in ihram and the woman in ihram, and the Muslim slave woman and the Scriptural woman' and the worship of stars. So if she acknowledges a book while worshipping stars, is her marriage permissible? They differed about it. And what was mentioned about marriage of a Scriptural woman absolutely implies permissibility of her marriage. He said: 'from the People of the Book' is reported from Abu al-Aliyah: 'The Sabians are a sect of the People of the Book who read the Psalms.' It was narrated by Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim, and Waki' narrated from al-Suddi: 'The Sabians are a group from the People of the Book.' And Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Jarir, and Ibn Abi Hatim narrated from Qatada: 'The Sabians worship angels, pray towards other than the qibla, and read the Psalms.' He said: 'and they have no book' is in agreement with what is narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'They are not Jews nor Christians, they are a people of polytheists; their slaughtered animals and marriages are not permissible.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. He said: 'his statement: his statement: his statement with nasb is object of 'atf, and the commentator explicitly stated it to remove the assumption that it is conjoined to 'worshipper of stars' falling under impermissibility. He said: 'and the marriage of the one in ihram and the woman in ihram' means the one who has entered ihram for Hajj or Umrah, and there is disagreement about it.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of marrying Sabian women. The author first establishes the general ruling: the People of the Book, despite their polytheistic beliefs (e.g., Trinity, Ezra as son of God), are permitted in marriage and consumption of their slaughtered animals based on the Quranic evidence, specifically Q. 2:221 which prohibits marrying polytheists but is interpreted as specific to non-Scriptural polytheists. The term 'shirk' when used absolutely in Shariah does not include the People of the Book. The commentary then explains the term 'al-Sabi'a', noting its linguistic root meaning 'to leave a religion'. It quotes al-Hidayah: marriage to Sabian women is permitted if they believe in a prophet and acknowledge a book, as they are then considered from the People of the Book. If they worship stars and have no book, marriage is prohibited because they are polytheists. The disagreement among scholars is based on the ambiguity of the Sabian sect; each scholar ruled according to the information available to him. The same ruling applies to their slaughtered animals. The author then clarifies that 'al-Mu'minah' is a clarifying description according to Abu Hanifa but a restrictive condition according to others. 'Without a book' indicates two conditions for prohibition: lack of a book and worship of stars. The core of the passage is the direct statement: 'Know that the marriage of a Sabian woman is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, not according to the two companions.' This disagreement stems from their interpretation of who the Sabians are. Abu Hanifa considers them from the People of the Book, hence permissible. The two companions consider them star-worshippers with no book, hence impermissible. The text then addresses a subsidiary issue: if a woman acknowledges a book but worships stars, there is disagreement, but the implication from earlier is permissibility. The commentary supports Abu Hanifa's view with narrations from Abu al-Aliyah, al-Suddi, and Qatada that Sabians are from the People of the Book and read the Psalms. It contrasts with the report from Ibn Abbas that they are polytheists without book, thus their slaughter and marriage are impermissible. Finally, the author notes a grammatical point to avoid misinterpretation and mentions the ruling on marriage of those in ihram, indicating that this topic is also subject to disagreement.

Key Terms
الصابئة (al-Ṣābi'a): A religious group that Abu Hanifa considers from the People of the Book if they believe in a prophet and a book; otherwise star-worshippers without scripture.
أهل الكتاب (Ahl al-Kitāb): People who possess a revealed scripture; in this context, those who follow a prophet and a book, which includes Sabians according to Abu Hanifa.
نكاح (nikāḥ): Marriage contract; the legal ruling on its permissibility with Sabian women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa permitting marriage with a Sabian woman?
A) Because Sabians are considered Muslims.
B) Because they are considered from the People of the Book.
C) Because they are not polytheists.
D) Because they follow the religion of the Sabi.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of marrying a Sabian woman in the Hanafi school hinges on her classification: Abu Hanifa considers her permissible if she affirms a prophet and book, while the Sahibayn prohibit her as a polytheist.

Ruling on Marrying a Sabian Woman: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Sabian marital status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding marriage to Sabian women and identify the basis for their ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The marriage of a Sabian woman is permissible (Abu Hanifa) or prohibited (Sahibayn) depending on whether Sabians are considered Ahl al-Kitab.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the marital eligibility of Sabian women. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of the term 'Sabian' and whether they belong to the People of the Book. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi ruling in real-world cases, as it shows how a single difference in scriptural classification can alter a legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi imam's position
Abu Hanifa holds that marriage to a Sabian woman is permissible because he considers Sabians to be from the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab).
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that such marriage is not permissible because they consider Sabians to be idol-worshippers without a revealed book.
3
Identify the basis of disagreement
The ikhtilaf is based on the interpretation of the term 'Sabian': Is it a scriptural community or a star-worshipping group?
This is a qualification dispute over the definition of 'Sabian'.
4
Analyse the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether a Muslim man may marry a Sabian woman. This directly affects actual marriage contracts.
5
Consider the special case of a woman acknowledging a book
The text raises the question of a woman who acknowledges a book yet worships idols; the implication tends towards permissibility, but there is ikhtilaf among the imams.
The outcome depends on how her 'acknowledgment of a book' is assessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن نكاح الصابئة يحل عند أبي حنيفة له ، لا عندهما، فقيل : هذا الخلافُ بناء على تفسير الصابئي ، فأبو حنيفة الا الله زعم أنَّ الصابئي من أهل الكتاب، فإن كان كذلك يجوز نكاحُ الصَّابئة، وهما زعما أنه من عبدة الكواكب ولا كتاب لهم، فلو كان كذلك لا يحل نكاحها(۱). ثُمَّ عطف على نكاح الكتابية قوله: (ونكاحُ المحْرِمِ والمَحْرِمَة، والأمة المسلمة والكتابية) وعبادة الكواكب، فلو كانت مقرَّةً بكتاب عابدة للكواكب، هل يحل نكاحها ؟ اختلفوا فيه : ومقتضى ما مرَّ في نكاح الكتابية مطلقاً يقتضي جواز نكاحها.
Know that marriage of a Sabian woman is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, not according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It is said: this difference is based on the interpretation of 'Sabian'. Abu Hanifa claimed that a Sabian is from the People of the Book; if so, marrying a Sabian woman is permissible. The two claimed that he is an idol-worshipper and has no book; if so, marrying her is not permissible. Then he (the author) appended to the marriage of a Kitabi woman his statement: 'And marriage of the muhrim and muhrima, and of the Muslim female slave and the Kitabi female slave'—and idol-worship. So if she (a woman) acknowledges a book yet worships idols, is her marriage permissible? They differed. And the implication of what has passed concerning the marriage of a Kitabi woman in absolute terms necessitates permissibility of her marriage.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the marriage of a Sabian woman. The disagreement stems from the interpretation of who the Sabians are. Abu Hanifa considers them to be a scriptural community (Ahl al-Kitab), thus marriage with them is permissible. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider them idol-worshippers without a revealed book, thus marriage is not permissible. The commentator then links this to the case of a woman who acknowledges a book but also worships idols, noting that the default permissibility for marrying a Kitabi woman would also apply here, though there is ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
صابئة (Sābi'a): A religious group; disputed whether they are Ahl al-Kitab or idol-worshippers
أهل الكتاب (Ahl al-Kitāb): People who possess a revealed scripture (Jews, Christians, and according to Abu Hanifa, Sabians)
عبدة الكواكب ('Abadat al-Kawākib): Star-worshippers; considered idolaters without a book

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Whether the Sabians have a known prophet
D) Whether the Sabians pray towards the Kaaba

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of marrying a Sabian woman in the Hanafi school depends on whether she is considered from Ahl al-Kitab, a point of ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

The Validity of Marriage in Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of marriage during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on marriage during ihram and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, marriage in ihram is valid because the contract is not among the prohibitions of the sacred state.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a person in ihram contract a valid marriage? The answer hinges on the interpretation of prophetic traditions and the nature of prohibitions during the pilgrimage. You will analyze the proofs from both sides and understand the practical consequences of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling of the Hanafi school: marriage in ihram is permissible and valid. The muhrim (person in ihram) may contract a marriage, though physical intimacy remains prohibited.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Recognize that the Shafi'i school holds the opposite: marriage is invalid during ihram. They base this on a clear prophetic command.
The Shafi'i position is presented first in the passage.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Study the Shafi'i evidence: the marfu' hadith 'The muhrim should not marry nor be married' and the action of Caliph Umar who annulled such a marriage.
This is a hadith qawli (verbal), which according to usul takes precedence over actions when there is conflict.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis counter: they rely on the action of Ibn Abbas marrying Maymuna while in ihram, and use qiyas (analogy) with other verbal contracts like purchasing a slave-girl for concubinage. They argue that marriage is permissible because the muhrim is only prohibited from physical acts, not contracts.
The commentator acknowledges the strength of the Shafi'i argument but adheres to the Hanafi view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a muhrim marries, the marriage is valid according to Hanafis but invalid according to Shafi'is. This affects the necessity of repeating the contract after ihram and the status of children.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيه: الشافعي، فعنده لا يجوز للمحرم والمحرمة في حالة الإحرام لما أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة ومسلم وغيرهم مرفوعاً: لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح، وروى مالك في الموطأ: «إن طريفاً تزوج امرأة وهو محرم، فردَّ عمر بن الخطاب نكاحه، وأجازه أصحابنا أخذاً بما روى الأئمة الستة وغيرهم عن ابن عباس: «إنه تزوج ميمونة وهو محرم»، وهو مؤيد بالقياس أيضاً، فإن النكاح مثل سائر العقود التي يتلفظ بها، والمحرم ليس بممنوع عن شيء منها حتى يجوز له شراء الأمة للتسري، غاية ما في الباب أنه لا يجوز المس أو التقبيل وغيرهما من محظورات الإحرام. ولا يخفى على الفطن أن مذهب الشافعي له قوي، كيف لا؟ فإن الحديث القولي يقدم على الفعلي عند التعارض مع أن تزوجه لميمونة مختلف فيه، فإنه روى الترمذي وأبو داود عن ميمونة رضي الله عنها: «أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم تزوجها، وهو حلال»، وأخرج الترمذي وأحمد وغيرهما عن أبي رافع كذلك وكان سفيراً بينهما، وأخرج الطحاوي عن يزيد بن الأصم وهو ابن أخت ميمونة رضي الله عنها، كما أن ابن عباس ابن أختها كذلك. وأسند أبو داود عن سعيد بن المسيب أن ابن عباس: «وَهِمَ في قوله: تزوجها وهو محرم»، وقد بسطتُ الكلام في المسألة في «التعليق الممجد على موطأ الإمام محمد».
And in it: Al-Shafi'i, for according to him it is not permissible for a muhrim and muhrima in the state of ihram, due to what the authors of the four Sunan, Muslim, and others narrated as a marfu' hadith: 'The muhrim should not marry nor be married.' And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta: 'That Tarif married a woman while he was in ihram, and Umar ibn al-Khattab annulled his marriage.' And our companions permitted it, taking what the six Imams and others narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'That he married Maymuna while he was in ihram.' And it is also supported by qiyas (analogy), for marriage is like other verbal contracts, and the muhrim is not prohibited from any of them, so he is even allowed to purchase a slave-girl for concubinage. The most that can be said is that touching, kissing, and other prohibitions of ihram are not allowed. And it is not hidden from the intelligent that the madhhab of al-Shafi'i is strong. How could it not be? For the verbal hadith takes precedence over the action when they conflict, especially since his marriage to Maymuna is disputed. For al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud narrated from Maymuna that he married her while he was halal (non-muhrim). And al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and others narrated from Abu Rafi' similarly, and he was the go-between. And al-Tahawi narrated from Yazid ibn al-Asamm, who is the nephew of Maymuna, just as Ibn Abbas is also her nephew. And Abu Dawud narrated from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that Ibn Abbas was mistaken in his statement that he married her while he was muhrim. And I have elaborated on the issue in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether a person in ihram can contract marriage. The Shafi'i position prohibits it based on the explicit hadith 'The muhrim should not marry nor be married' and the practice of Umar annulling such a marriage. The Hanafi position permits it, relying on the action of Ibn Abbas who married Maymuna while in ihram, and on qiyas (analogy) with other verbal contracts like purchase which are allowed for the muhrim. The commentator acknowledges the strength of the Shafi'i argument, noting the principle that a verbal prohibition (hadith qawli) takes precedence over an action (hadith fi'li) when they conflict. He also mentions that the marriage to Maymuna is disputed: some narrations state the Prophet was not in ihram, and Ibn Abbas's memory is questioned. The author refers to his own work for a fuller treatment.

Key Terms
محرم (Muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah
إحرام (Iḥrām): The sacred state of pilgrimage with certain prohibitions
حديث قولي (Ḥadīth Qawlī): A hadith containing a verbal command or prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi evidence for permitting marriage in ihram?
A) A hadith stating the Prophet himself married while in ihram
B) The practice of Ibn Abbas marrying Maymuna while in ihram
C) The principle that all contracts are forbidden in ihram except marriage
D) The consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage in ihram based on companion practice and analogy, while the Shafi'i school prohibits it based on a clear prophetic hadith; the difference lies in how each school weighs evidence.

Marriage During Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi response to Shafi'i prohibition of marriage in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on marriage during ihram by comparing their respective proofs and identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The Prophet's action trumps his words: Hanafis permit marriage in ihram despite the verbal prohibition.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i disagreement over the validity of marriage while in ihram. The Hanafi school relies on the Prophet's own example and analogical reasoning, while the Shafi'i school prioritizes a direct prohibition. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school resolves apparent conflicts between textual evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i position is based on the hadith 'la yankih al-muhrim wa la yunkah' (the muhrim should not marry nor be married), reported by the four Sunan and Muslim, and the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab who annulled a marriage contracted in ihram.
This is a qawli (verbal) hadith directly prohibiting the act.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (ﷺ) married Maimuna while in ihram, and on qiyas (analogy) with other contracts like purchasing a slave girl, which is permissible in ihram.
This is a fi'li (actual practice) hadith demonstrating permissibility.
3
Analyze the conflict of proofs
When a qawli hadith conflicts with a fi'li hadith, the Hanafi school gives precedence to the action (fi'l) because it is more explicit in demonstrating permissibility. The verbal hadith is interpreted as referring to the prohibition of intimacy, not the contract itself.
This is a key usul principle: action can specify or restrict a general prohibition.
4
Note the factual dispute
Some narrations state that the Prophet married Maimuna while halal (not in ihram). The Hanafis acknowledge this but maintain that the stronger narrations support the ihram version, and the action of the Prophet takes precedence over sayings that might be subject to interpretation.
This shows the importance of riwayah evaluation in inter-madhhab disputes.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'is require the couple to separate or renew the marriage after ihram, while Hanafis consider the marriage valid as is, with the only restriction being physical intimacy during ihram.
This difference directly affects the legal status of the couple's relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشافعي ، فعنده لا يجوز للمحرم والمحرمة في حالة الإحرام لما أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة ومسلم وغيرهم مرفوعاً : لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح ، وروى مالك في الموطأ : «إن طريفاً تزوج امرأة وهو محرم، فردَّ عمر بن الخطاب الله نكاحه (٢) وأجازه أصحابنا أخذاً بما روى الأئمة الستة وغيرهم عن ابن عباس : «إنه تزوج ميمونة وهو محرم (٣)، وهو مؤيد بالقياس أيضاً، فإن النكاح مثل سائر العقود التي يتلفظ بها، والمحرم ليس بممنوع عن شيء منها حتى يجوز له شراء الأمة للتسري ، غاية ما في الباب أنه لا يجوز المس أو التقبيل وغيرهما من محظورات الإحرام. ولا يخفى على الفطن أن مذهب الشافعي له قوي، كيف لا ؟ فإن الحديث القولي يقدم على الفعلي عند التعارض مع أن تزوجه له ميمونة مختلف فيه ، فإنه روى الترمذي وأبو داود عن ميمونة رضي الله عنها : «أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم تزوجها، وهو حلال» (٤) وأخرج الترمذي وأحمد وغيرهما عن أبي رافع كذلك وكان سفيراً بينهما ، وأخرج الطحاوي عن يزيد بن الأصم وهو ابن أخت ميمونة رضي الله عنها، كما أن ابن عباس ابن أختها كذلك. وأسند أبو داود عن سعيد بن المسيب له أن ابن عباس : «وَهِمَ في قوله : تزوجها وهو محرم)، وقد بسطتُ الكلام في المسألة في «التعليق الممجـد علـى موطأ الإمام محمد )
Al-Shafi'i holds that it is not permissible for a man or woman in ihram to marry, because of what the authors of the four Sunan, Muslim, and others reported as a marfu' hadith: 'The muhrim should not marry nor be married.' Malik reported in the Muwatta' that Tarif married a woman while in ihram, and Umar ibn al-Khattab annulled the marriage. Our companions allowed it, based on what the six Imams and others narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'He married Maimuna while in ihram.' It is also supported by qiyas, since marriage is like other contracts that are verbalized, and the muhrim is not prevented from any of them; rather, he is allowed to purchase a slave girl for concubinage. The most that can be said is that touching, kissing, and other ihram prohibitions are not allowed. It is not hidden from the intelligent that the Shafi'i school is strong; how could it not be, since the verbal hadith is given precedence over the practical one when they conflict, especially since the Prophet's marriage to Maimuna is disputed. For al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud narrated from Maimuna that the Prophet married her while he was halal. Al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and others narrated from Abu Rafi' similarly, and he was the intermediary. Al-Tahawi narrated from Yazid ibn al-Asamm, who is Maimuna's nephew, and Ibn Abbas is also her nephew. Abu Dawud narrated from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab that Ibn Abbas was mistaken in saying 'he married her while in ihram.' I have discussed the matter extensively in 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad 'ala Muwatta' al-Imam Muhammad'.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of marriage while in ihram. The commentator presents the Shafi'i position based on the hadith 'la yankih al-muhrim' and the practice of Umar, and then presents the Hanafi position based on the action of the Prophet marrying Maimuna in ihram and qiyas to other contracts. The commentator acknowledges the strength of the Shafi'i argument but maintains the Hanafi view that the marriage is valid, though physical intimacy is prohibited during ihram. The disagreement over the authenticity of the Prophet's marriage to Maimuna while in ihram is also noted, with some narrations stating he was halal. The passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of preferring actual practice (fi'li) over verbal hadith (qawli) in case of conflict, and the use of qiyas to analogize marriage to other permissible contracts.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is makruh but still valid.

The Hanafi school permits marriage in ihram based on the Prophet's action and qiyas, distinguishing the contract from prohibited physical acts.

Nikah — Marriage

Marrying Slave Women: Hanafi Response to Shafi'i on Specification by Description and Conditioning
Commentary on Wiqayah explaining the Hanafi view in dispute with Shafi'i on two issues from Quran 4:25.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on marrying believing slave women when able to afford a free woman, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principles of takhsis bi al-wasf and ta'liq bi al-shart.

Core Idea
Description does not necessarily restrict, and condition does not imply its opposite – Hanafi usul in action.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' presents the Hanafi commentary on a key verse (Quran 4:25) regarding the permissibility of marrying slave women. It engages with Imam al-Shafi'i's objections based on two usul principles: specification by description and conditioning. By understanding this dispute, you will see how usul al-fiqh principles directly shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contested issues
The passage discusses two issues: (1) does the description 'believing' in the verse restrict permissibility to believing slave women only? (2) does the condition of lacking 'tawl' imply prohibition when one has 'tawl'?
These arise from the same verse but involve different usul principles.
2
Examine the Shafi'i arguments
For each issue, note al-Shafi'i's reliance on takhsis bi al-wasf and ta'liq bi al-shart. He argues that the description negates the ruling for non-believing slave women, and the condition implies the opposite when the condition is absent.
Al-Shafi'i provides the example of 'the tall man does not fly' to illustrate his understanding of urf.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttals
The Hanafi response: description may be incidental (for emphasis or praise) and does not necessarily negate; conditioning only ties the ruling to the condition, not the opposite. The verse is silent on cases outside the condition.
Hanafis point out that rational people find 'the tall man does not run' ugly, showing that specification by description is not universally negating.
4
Connect the usul principles to the thamarah al-khilaf
How do these differing usul positions translate into different practical rulings? For the first issue: Hanafi permits marrying Kitabiyya slave women; Shafi'i forbids. For the second: Hanafi permits marrying a slave woman even with tawl; Shafi'i forbids.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the concrete difference in permissible marriages.
5
Locate the mufta bihi position
The text and footnotes indicate that the Hanafi position is the operative ruling (mufta bihi). Marrying a slave woman when able to marry a free woman is permissible but better avoided; marrying a non-believing slave woman is also permissible according to Hanafi usul.
The mufta bihi relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah and later tarjih.

Book of Marriage, Chapter of Prohibited Women: 49. The disagreement of al-Shafi'i, based on the principle that specification by description necessitates negation of the ruling from what is other than it according to him, not according to us. So His statement 'from your believing slave girls' negates the permissibility of marrying the Kitabiyya according to him. ... And also with the capacity (to marry) a free woman: the meaning of 'capacity of a free woman' is the ability to marry her, meaning having the dower and maintenance of a free woman. And there is disagreement of al-Shafi'i based on the principle that conditioning with a condition necessitates non-existence when the condition is absent. ... But according to us, it is silent about this ruling. And according to us: conditioning with a condition only indicates the binding of that part to that condition, not its non-existence when it is absent. So with us, marrying a slave woman is permissible absolutely.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' is a commentary on the Wiqayah, explaining the Hanafi position in a disagreement with al-Shafi'i regarding two related issues arising from Quran 4:25. The first issue: does the verse's description of slave women as 'believing' ('min fatayatimu al-mu'minat') exclude non-believing slave women from permissibility of marriage? Al-Shafi'i argues that specification by description ('takhsis bi al-wasf') negates the ruling from anything lacking that description, so only believing slave women are permissible. The Hanafi school responds that such specification does not necessarily negate; the description may be incidental or for emphasis, not as a condition. The second issue: does the verse's condition 'if you cannot afford to marry free believing women' imply that marrying a slave woman is forbidden when one can afford a free woman? Al-Shafi'i says yes, because conditioning a ruling on a condition implies its opposite when the condition is absent. The Hanafis state that the verse is silent about this; conditioning only ties the ruling to that condition, not its opposite. Thus, in the Hanafi madhhab, marrying a believing slave woman is permissible even if one can afford a free woman, and marrying a non-believing slave woman is also permissible (though the permissibility of Kitabiyya is subject to other discussions). The text also defines 'tawl' as the ability to provide dower and maintenance. The commentary emphasizes that the detailed proofs are found in works of usul al-fiqh like 'al-Tawdih' and its gloss 'al-Talwih'. This passage thus clarifies key principles of Hanafi usul al-fiqh that underpin branch rulings in nikah.

Key Terms
الطول (al-tawl): Capacity and ability (financial) to marry a free woman, specifically possessing her dower (mahr) and the means to provide for her maintenance (nafaqah).
التخصيص بالوصف (al-takhsis bi al-wasf): A principle of interpretation: specifying a ruling by attaching a description (adjective) to the subject. The debate is whether this implies that the ruling is limited to only those with that description.
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): Conditioning a ruling on the existence of a condition. The dispute is whether this also implies the opposite ruling when the condition is absent (mafhum al-mukhalafah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling for a free man who has the financial means (tawl) to marry a free woman but wishes to marry a believing slave woman?
A) It is forbidden (haram).
B) It is permissible (mubah), but it is better not to do so.
C) It is mandatory (wajib) to marry a slave woman to lower sin.
D) It is only permissible if he fears committing sin (zina).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes itself from al-Shafi'i by holding that specification by description and conditioning do not automatically negate the ruling for non-described or non-conditioned cases; this usul difference yields distinct practical rulings on marrying slave women.

Nikah — Marriage
